## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material, which is central to constitutive modeling in materials science. Temperature typically modifies elastic stiffness and hardening behavior, while strain governs the mechanical response through linear or nonlinear relationships.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic stress-strain at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - T) (linear elasticity with thermal softening of modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear plastic stress-strain relationship)
- Ramberg-Osgood type: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic with power-law hardening)
- Johnson-Cook type (no strain rate): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T**c5) (thermo-mechanical hardening with thermal softening)
- Thermal softening power law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (power-law hardening with exponential thermal effect)
- Linear thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 - c1 * T) (modulus decreasing linearly with temperature)
- Arrhenius-type thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 / T) (thermally activated deformation mechanism)
- Polynomial hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (polynomial stress-strain curve)
- Voce-type saturation hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * (c2 - c3 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal softening)
- Ludwik model with temperature: sigma = c0 * (c1 - c2 * T) + c3 * epsilon**c4 (yield stress + power hardening, T-dependent yield)
- Hyperbolic tangent hardening: sigma = c0 * tanh(c1 * epsilon) * (c2 - c3 * T) (saturating hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Bilinear with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**c3 (temperature-dependent modulus plus nonlinear hardening)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening of elastic modulus → Multiplicative factor (c0 - c1*T) or (1 - c1*T/c2) on strain-dependent terms
- Power-law strain hardening → epsilon**c with 0 < c < 1 indicates work hardening in metals (Hollomon-type)
- Arrhenius-type temperature dependence → exp(c/T) suggests thermally activated dislocation mechanisms
- Saturation stress behavior → (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) form indicates Voce-type asymptotic hardening
- Separable thermo-mechanical response → sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T) suggests independent hardening and thermal softening mechanisms
- Homologous temperature scaling → T appears as (T_melt - T) or ratio form, reflecting distance from melting point
- Strain-temperature coupling → Terms like epsilon*T or epsilon**c1 * T**c2 indicate non-separable thermo-mechanical interaction
- Concave-up vs concave-down strain response → epsilon**c with c>1 (concave up) vs c<1 (concave down) distinguishes hardening regimes
